Dedicated to enhancing working conditions, workplace improvement committee collaborates with employee and 
worker representatives to identify and implement measures for improved comfort, working conditions, ergonomics 
and work-life balance. Himadri adheres to the SA 8000:2014 Management Standard, reflecting a deep commitment 
to social accountability and ethical practices. These protocols guarantee fair treatment, safe working conditions 
and respect for workers’ rights, including third-party personnel, covering crucial areas such as the prohibition of 
child labour, health and safety, fair remuneration and a reliable complaint mechanism.
	
As a forward looking organization, Himadri actively seeks to redress concerns raised by our employees/workers. 
However, since inception we have cultivated a culture of turning concerns into opportunities. It is one of the principle 
building-blocks of our company. We vigorously nurture open communication channels with our employees and 
workers and actively take part to develop plausible and sustainable solution.

15. 	 Details of any corrective action taken or underway 
to address safety-related incidents (if any) and on 
significant risks / concerns arising from assessments 
of health & safety practices and working conditions.
	
Himadri has a robust process for reporting near 
misses, accident or dangerous occurrences. We 
ensure all manufacturing plants report Lost Time 
Injuries (LTIs), Medically Treated Injuries (MTIs) and 
First Aid Cases (FACs) to maintain safety focus. 
Investigations extend to all the Near Misses, First Aid 
Cases, Dangerous Occurrences and MTIs. First aid 
cases and low severity DO's are solved using Line 
Practical Problem Solving tool, while MTI, RSI, LTI, and 
High Severity DO's cover process-related incidents 
using the 8D Practical Problem Solving tool. Himadri 
aims to reach an LTIFR below 1.0, ensuring employee 
safety and achieving zero accidents.

Empowering People through Safety Leadership and Problem-Solving at Himadri - At Himadri, we believe that 
cultivating a strong safety culture and building problem-solving capabilities are key drivers of operational 
excellence. In line with this vision, we have successfully trained over 200 employees under our Safety Leadership 
Program, empowering them to take ownership of safety, led by example, and provide a proactive safety mindset 
across teams.
	
In addition, our workforce has been equipped with critical thinking and analytical skills through training on the 8 
Dimensions of Practical Problem Solving. This structured approach enables our employees to identify root causes, 
implement sustainable solutions, and drive continuous improvement in their daily work.
	
These initiatives reflect our ongoing commitment to nurturing leaders at every level and creating a safer, smarter, 
and more resilient organization.

1.	
Does the entity extend any life insurance or any compensatory package in the event of death of (A) Employees 
(Y/N) (B) Workers (Y/N).

2.	
Provide the measures undertaken by the entity to ensure that statutory dues have been deducted and deposited 
by the value chain partners.
	
During the contract with value chain partners [suppliers & vendors] the company ensures that there is provision 
of compliance with terms and conditions, including all the applicable laws of the land. Moreover, for contracts 
related to manpower supply, the company has implemented a robust system which cross-checks to ensure that 
all statutory dues are accurately deducted and deposited. Himadri is committed to fostering transparency, ethical 
practices, and compliance throughout its value chain, including upstream and downstream third party partners like 
agents, consultants, and distributors. The Due Diligence Programme ensures that all partners align with Himadri’s 
sustainability objectives and adhere to global standards of governance, social responsibility, and environmental 
impact mitigation. This structured programme evaluates partners on critical elements, including anti-bribery, 
anti-corruption, prevention of child and forced labor, anti-tax evasion, and data security. It involves a systematic 
process of assessment, categorisation, monitoring, and continuous improvement to mitigate risks while promoting 
ethical and sustainable practices.  The programme ensures partners comply with tax regulations and demonstrate 
ethical financial practices. Measures include:
 
 
Validation of partners’ tax filings and compliance records.
 
 
Monitoring for any discrepancies in financial transactions or reporting.
 
 
Training sessions for partners on the importance of adhering to anti-tax evasion norms.
 
 
Offering training sessions on adherence to anti-tax evasion norms.

Himadri’s commitment to workplace safety extends beyond its direct employees, incorporating a comprehensive 
contractor safety management protocol designed to protect all non-employee workers (including third party) on 
site. This protocol is rooted in rigorous standards that cover multiple aspects of health and safety to ensure a safe, 
compliant and efficient work environment for contractors.
	
The contractor safety management protocol includes specific standards for Contractor Safety, Workplace Risk 
Assessment, Workplace Stress Management, Health and Safety Training, HSE Audit & Inspection and Hazardous 
Chemical Handling. Each standard is meticulously designed to address critical safety concerns and implementation 
of high safety standards. The protocol ensures that all contractors are thoroughly trained on safety procedures 
relevant to their roles and responsibilities. This training includes modules on handling hazardous materials, 
understanding workplace hazards.

to

towards

As part of its commitment to contract safety 
management, Himadri ensures that all third-party 
workers undergo 100% induction training before 
their engagement on the shop floor. This training 
provides essential knowledge on safety protocols, 
operational procedures and risk mitigation measures 
specific to the work environment and actions during 
Emergency situations. By equipping third-party 
personnel with the necessary skills and awareness 
we provide a culture of safety, reduce the likelihood 
of incidents and maintain a safe and compliant 
workplace for everyone involved.

Himadri’s Code of Conduct for Suppliers enshrines 
the Company’s unwavering focus on fair treatment, 
human rights, gender diversity, child labour, wages, 
working hours, occupational health, safety & the 
environment. The Code upholds the spirit outlined 
in the International Labour Organisation Guidelines 
and United Nations Guiding Principles on Business 
and Human Rights and is shared and accepted by 
all supply chain partners. The Company has a robust 
process of evaluating its suppliers and service 
providers before engaging with them, proactively 
making them aware of its expectations/ requirements, 
and seeking commitment for compliance through 
contractual agreements. We are equally dedicated 
to strengthening awareness of this Code among 
our suppliers and service providers and providing 
support to aid them in this initiative.
	
Though we have engaged our upstream value chain 
partners – supplier, raw material consumables and 
service vendors, moving forward we have an action 
plan to engage our downstream value chain partners 
– customers and business partners as well.

Principle 4
Businesses should respect the interests of and be responsive to all its 
stakeholders
SDGs Impacted
Sustainable businesses have an inherent duty to protect the interests 
of their stakeholders, including vulnerable and marginalized groups. 
Such organizations must deliver on their responsibility to maximize the 
positive impact of their activities, products, processes, and decisions 
for their stakeholders.
Himadri is acclaimed for its dedication to safeguarding stakeholder 
interests, optimizing shared value and harmonizing business 
objectives with stakeholder expectations. The Company interacts 
with stakeholders regularly to gather constructive feedback, which 
serves as an invaluable input for enhancing business decisions and 
fostering positive impacts. These engagements enable the Company 
to systematically address stakeholder concerns through structured 
processes.

Leadership Indicators
1.	
Provide the processes for consultation between 
stakeholders 
and 
the 
Board 
on 
economic, 
environmental, and social topics or if consultation is 
delegated, how is feedback from such consultations 
provided to the Board.
	
ESG priorities in the Company are driven from 
the uppermost level i.e., the Board of Directors. 
The Board provides the strategic oversight and 
has constituted an ESG Committee to provide 
guidance and monitor the ESG progress. The ESG 
Committee of the Board has delegated the process 
of undertaking consultations with stakeholders to 
the management. Feedback from such consultations 
is shared with the Committee and the Board. 
Himadri has undertaken a comprehensive materiality 
assessment and stakeholder engagement exercise 
to identify Environmental, Social and Governance 
(ESG) topics of significance. As a part of this 
exercise, Himadri along with an external agency, 
with requisite experience, engaged with the key 
internal and external stakeholders to understand 
their concerns and incorporate their views into 
materiality assessment, for prioritizing ESG topics 
and 
frameworks. 
Insights 
gathered 
through 
stakeholder engagement were analysed to develop 
the materiality matrix and arrive at the final list of 
ESG focus areas. The result of this assessment was 
presented to the ESG Committee and the Board. 
The outcome is being considered for defining ESG 
objectives of the Company.

Principle 5
Businesses should respect and promote human rights
SDGs Impacted
Businesses must operate in a manner that respects and upholds 
the inherent rights and entitlement of individuals without any 
discrimination. The core tenets of this principle are based on the 
Constitution of India and international Human Rights standards 
such as the International Bill of Rights and UN Guiding Principles on 
Business and Human Rights. 
Equal human right is a fundamental aspect of the Company’s business 
ethics and operational framework, which encompasses its policies, 
processes and practices. The Company’s commitment and respect for 
human rights is translated in its publicly accessible policies, including 
‘Labour and Human rights policy, ‘Code of Conduct’. For Himadri, "dignity 
at work" is not just a commitment but a way of business conduct.

4.	
Do you have a focal point (Individual/ Committee) 
responsible for addressing human rights impacts 
or issues caused or contributed to by the business? 
(Yes/No)
	
Yes, Himadri is committed to fostering a work 
environment grounded in respect, dignity, and 
fairness. In alignment with this ethos, the Company 
has established a robust Whistle Blower and 
Human Rights Grievance Mechanism that serves 
as a focal point for addressing concerns, including 
those related to human rights violations caused or 
contributed to by the business.
	
The Company encourages an open-door policy, 
promoting transparency and accessibility across all 
levels. Employees and associates are empowered to 
raise grievances or report any form of misconduct, 
without fear of retaliation, through multiple safe 
channels.
	
Key Features of the Mechanism:
 
 
Reporting Channels: Employees and associates 
may report grievances or violations to the 
Human 
Resource 
department 
or 
Senior 
Management. The Company strictly prohibits 
any form of reprisal or retaliatory action against 
individuals raising concerns in good faith.
 
 
Investigation and Redressal: Where necessary, 
a dedicated investigation committee is formed 
to evaluate reported violations. In collaboration 
with 
Senior 
Management, 
the 
committee 
ensures prompt resolution and implements 
appropriate remedial actions.
 
 
Human Rights Due Diligence: The Company 
periodically 
conducts 
human 
rights 
due 
diligence, monitoring the effectiveness of its 
policies and identifying potential areas for 
improvement in its governance framework.
 
 
Prevention of Sexual Harassment (POSH): 
Himadri has a clearly defined POSH Policy 
to prevent and address any form of sexual 
harassment at the workplace. Concerns under 
this category can also be reported through the 
established grievance mechanisms.
5.	
Describe the internal mechanisms in place to redress 
grievances related to human rights issues.
	
In this regard the Company encourages an open-door 
policy. The Company has built a strong mechanism 
for reporting matters or concerns faced at the 
workplace. Himadri recognises the importance that 
business can play in ensuring long term protection 
of human rights and for this reason the company 
is dedicated to upholding the human rights of its 
employees, communities.
	
The mechanism is outlined below:
	
1. 	
The employees/ associates can address their 
complaints or grievances or report instances 
to the Human Resource department/ Senior 
Management. No reprisal or retaliatory action 
is taken against any employee/ associates for 
raising concerns under this policy.
	
2. 	
If the situation warrants, a committee is formed 
to investigate the violations reported. The 
Committee evaluates the violations reported 
and ensures that the same are addressed and 
resolved at the earliest. The Committee also, 
in consultation with the Senior Management, 
provides a suitable remedy.
	
3. 	
The Company periodically undertakes human 
rights due diligence process for management 
and oversight/ monitoring of the policy and 
identifies any shortcomings.
	
4. 	
The Company also has a Policy on Prevention 
of Sexual Harassment (POSH), and any such 
concern can be reported.

Whistleblowing can be used when individuals, such as directors, employees, 
or any other stakeholders, have genuine concerns or grievances related to 
the following issues: 
Unethical behaviour: 
Reporting any action that goes against ethical standards or the code of conduct of the company. 
Fraud: 
Reporting actual or suspected fraudulent activities within the organization. 
Violation of the Code of Conduct or Policy: 
Reporting any breaches of the company's code of conduct or policy. 
Breach of business integrity and ethics: 
Reporting actions that compromise business integrity or ethical practices. 
Intentional financial irregularities: 
Reporting instances of intentional financial mismanagement, including fraud. 
Deliberate violation of laws/regulations: 
Reporting actions that violate laws or regulations. 
Gross or willful negligence causing danger: 
Reporting actions that pose substantial and specific danger to health, safety, and the environment. 
Manipulation of company data/records: 
Reporting any attempts to manipulate or falsify company data or records. 
Pilferage of confidential/proprietary information: 
Reporting unauthorized access or use of confidential company information. 
Gross wastage/misappropriation of company funds/assets: 
Reporting instances of significant misuse or misappropriation of company funds or assets. 
Whistleblowing concerns can be reported to speakup@himadri.com 
The Name of the Complainee will be kept confidential, during and post procedures. There will be no reciprocal impact on the Complainee.

the

external 
experts 
(legal,

inducted.
	
Thorough Investigation
 
 
Detailed fact-finding with evidence collection, 
interviews, and document review.
 
 
The process ensures impartiality and non-
retaliation.
	
Decision Making
 
 
After analyzing all facts, a conclusion is drawn.
 
 
If the concern is valid, corrective and preventive 
actions are taken.
 
 
If unsubstantiated, the rationale is documented 
and communicated respectfully.
	
Resolution and Remedy
 
 
Remedies are implemented in consultation with 
senior management.
	
May include:
 
 
Disciplinary action
 
 
Policy revisions
 
 
Victim support
 
 
Workplace safety improvements
 
 
Awareness and training sessions
	
Documentation and Reporting
 
 
All cases are documented and tracked.
 
 
Trends are analyzed to strengthen systems and 
prevent recurrence.

Himadri actively fosters a workplace culture where diversity is embraced, and inclusivity is woven into everyday 
operations. Employees are encouraged to engage in meaningful dialogue that promotes empathy, understanding, 
and mutual respect—strengthening the social fabric of the organization.
	
In line with its commitment to human rights and ethical conduct, Himadri has established a strong Prevention of 
Sexual Harassment (POSH) Policy. The policy enforces a zero-tolerance approach to harassment and is aligned with 
national legal frameworks. It aims to create a safe, respectful, and inclusive work environment for all employees.
	
To ensure robust implementation, an Internal Complaints Committee (ICC) is in place, functioning with complete 
confidentiality and impartiality. The ICC not only addresses reported incidents but also conducts awareness 
sessions and regular training to help employees identify and prevent harassment. These efforts are integral to 
building a workplace rooted in accountability, dignity, and psychological safety.
	
Himadri’s proactive stance on POSH and inclusive culture reflects its broader commitment to employee well-being, 
social equity, and sustainable corporate responsibility.

8.	
Mechanisms to prevent adverse consequences to the 
complainant in discrimination and harassment cases.
	
The Grievance Redressal Policy clearly outlines that 
all members involved as a part of the enquiry are 
entrusted to keep record in a confidential manner. 
Any employee questioned in respect of the enquiry 
is bound by confidentiality and is required to keep all 
paperwork and information exchanged in the process 
confidential and such practices are followed also 
while handling and assessing complaints which form 
a part of the grievance redressal mechanism.
	
All genuine complaints, in good faith, can be made 
without fear of reprisals, punishment, intimidation, 
coercive action, dismissal, or victimization. All actual 
violations are dealt seriously on the principles of natural

9.	
Do human rights requirements form part of your 
business agreements and contracts? (Yes/No)
	
Yes, Himadri integrates human rights requirements 
into its Supplier Code of Conduct, ensuring that 
all suppliers respect and uphold internationally 
recognized human rights standards. The Company 
strictly prohibits any form of forced, child, or 
compulsory labour, and expects its suppliers to 
demonstrate full compliance across their operations.
	
To participate in Himadri’s value chain, suppliers 
must adhere to the Supplier Code of Conduct, which 
is aligned with key global frameworks including 
the United Nations Declaration on Human Rights 
(UDHR), ILO’s Declaration on Fundamental Principles 
and Rights at Work, IFC Performance Standards, and 
the UN Guiding Principles on Business and Human 
Rights (UNGPs).
	
As part of its Sustainable Supply Chain Framework, 
Himadri also mandates supplier audits, where buyers 
evaluate vendors on critical sustainability criteria, 
including but not Limited to human rights and labour 
rights. This ensures proactive due diligence and 
fosters accountability throughout the supply network.

Our energy management and GHG emission policy 
are in place to drive our initiatives for attaining our 
sustainable goals. Himadri continues to optimize 
energy 
use 
through 
the 
implementation 
of 
ISO 50001:2018 standards and advanced monitoring 
technologies. Initiatives like capturing and reusing 
system, 
transforming 
to 
fuel 
diversification, 
optimizing process and operation all these contribute 
to keep energy consumption in check.
	
We are tirelessly endeavoring through our efforts to 
optimize energy consumption reducing associated 
environmental footprint. Therefore, ISO 50001:2018 
energy management system is applied in all of our plant 
locations. As a result, BU level “Energy Optimization 
Task Force” has been formed to drive our initiatives 
efficiently. Focused on energy-saving opportunities 
and implementing cutting-edge technologies, this task 
force ensures that the Company minimizes energy 
consumption while maintaining operational excellence.
	
Himadri is dedicated to promote sustainable practices, 
committed to a Net-zero vision aligned with India’s 
Net-zero goal, validated by the Science Based Targets 
initiative (SBTi) for 2050. Our efforts align with the 
principles of UNGC; and SDG 13 (Climate Action). 
Participation in the Taskforce on Climate-related 
Financial Disclosures (TCFD) and Carbon Disclosure 
Project (CDP) highlights its commitment to manage 
climate related risks and explore environmental 
stewardship opportunities. 
	
At Himadri we consider energy management as 
a mainstream responsibility and all stakeholders 
are accountable for managing and monitoring 
energy consumptions. Himadri embarked on the 
implementation of a digital energy management 
system at the Carbon Black Division in Mahistikry.
	
The Company installed the SmartComm software 
by L&T Electrical and Automation directed to 
manage energy consumption. At the Carbon Black 
division, 140 smart meters were installed in the 
generating unit and process distribution sections / 
subsections. These meters monitor auxiliary power 
consumption trends and an easy analysis of specific 
energy consumption across processes. This energy 
consumption data consists of attributes towards 
chemical plants’ production as well as auxiliary fuel 
consumption such as DG sets etc. 
	
Our captive power plant uses generated waste gas 
from Carbon black manufacturing process to make 
and meet the in house energy necessity. This data is 
verified through energy audits. Energy consumption 
and efficiency metrics are reviewed to ensure 
progress in reducing overall environmental impact 
through energy management initiatives. 
	
These establish our continuous efforts of adhering 
to our sustainability objective to reduce energy 
intensity, there by minimizing impacts and serving 
towards our goal of emerging as environmentally 
driven entity.
 	
Initiative related to energy consumption reduction: 
 
 
Hot air line insulation improvement in RX-A & C to 
reduce temp. drop by 20 DegC. This benefits in 
the reduction of process specific energy intensity.
 
 
The project aims to incorporate deaerated 
hot water into Waste Heat Recovery Boilers 
(WHRBs), resulting in a projected steam 
generation increase of approximately 20-30%,

equivalent to about 24 TPD at a pressure of 
20 kg. The full integration of this system is 
expected to further optimize boiler efficiency, 
ensure greater reliability, and enhance energy 
recovery capabilities, significantly contributing 
to overall plant sustainability and performance 
goals.
 
 
Hot air line duct is activated which connects 
the line #3 secondary APH to the Boiler #3 
combustor. 
The 
secondary 
APH 
captures 
residual heat from dirty gas streams, raising the 
air temperature to 350°C. By redirecting this hot 
air to the boiler, the energy required to heat the 
combustion air is reduced. Ambient air (~25°C) 
requires more power from the FD fan to achieve 
combustion temperatures. Using preheated 
air reduces the temperature gradient, leading 
to lower fan energy requirements and also 
subsequently reducing the fuel consumption in 
the combustor.

Details of the following disclosures related to water:
	
Himadri is committed to sustainable water management, adopting advanced technologies and practices to 
reduce freshwater consumption, recycle wastewater and mitigate environmental impact. Himadri utilises the WRI 
Aqueduct tool to analyse physical risks such as water stress, flooding and water quality. The Company conducts 
water risk assessments based on water basins and site-specific water use.

Financial Statements
	
Himadri employs a multifaceted approach to reduce 
water withdrawals, integrating Rainwater Harvesting, 
Steam Condensation, Water Recovery through Water 
Recovery Plants (WRP), and Zero Liquid Discharge 
(ZLD) capacity expansion. We are committed in 
reducing daily water consumption by 20% within 
2026. Our Water Efficiency and Preservation 
Policy upholds our integrity towards delivering to 
a sustainable world. The pursuit of water positivity 
through a zero liquid discharge (ZLD) process helps 
moderate environment impact and enhance water 
resource sustainability. Our initiatives align with 
UNSDG 6 (Clean water and sanitation). 
	
In the fiscal year 2024-25,we achieved a significant 
reduction in our average daily water consumption 
which is a daily savings of 462KL
	
To accomplish this, we implemented several key 
initiatives:
	
•	
Arresting Steam Leakages: We focused on 
arresting 
steam 
leakages 
in 
the 
Captive 
Power Plant (CPP) and Central Boiler Division 
areas. This helped in reducing water loss and 
improving overall efficiency.
	
•	
Condenser Recovery System: We installed a 
condenser recovery system in the CPP, which 
allowed us to recover and reuse water that 
would otherwise be lost.
	
•	
Heat 
Exchanger 
in 
Blowdown 
Line: 
By 
integrating a heat exchanger in the blow down 
line of the CPP, we were able to recover heat and 
reduce water consumption for other processes.
	
•	
Minimizing Intermittent Blowdown (IBD) and 
Continuous Blowdown (CBD): We minimized 
the IBD (procedure to remove suspended 
solids, including any sludge formed in the 
boiler water) and CBD (continuous removal of a 
small amount of water from the boiler, typically 
from the surface, to control the concentration 
of Total Dissolved Solids (TDS) and maintain 
boiler water quality processes in the CPP as per 
water quality analysis, further reducing water 
wastage.
	
•	
Water Recovery System: We implemented a 
comprehensive water recovery system (New 
Water Recovery Plant) to reclaim and reuse 
water within our operations.
	
•	
Fill Pack Replacement: We replaced the fill 
pack in our cooling towers, which improved the 
efficiency of our cooling processes and reduced 
water usage.

Water discharged from industrial activities can 
significantly disrupt local eco-systems, harming 
aquatic life and affecting the livelihoods of 
surrounding communities due to contamination. At 
Himadri, we recognize this critical challenge and 
have taken proactive, responsible steps to safeguard 
our environment.
	
We have successfully implemented Zero Liquid 
Discharge (ZLD) across all our facilities, reinforcing 
our strong commitment to water conservation and 
ecosystem protection. This initiative ensures that no 
untreated or contaminated water is released into the 
environment, thereby eliminating the risk of polluting 
nearby water bodies.
	
Aligned with our Water Efficiency and Preservation 
Policy, this approach is a key pillar of our sustainability 
strategy. To drive this initiative further, Himadri has 
established a dedicated Zero Liquid Discharge Task 
Force at the Business Unit level. This task force leads 
the way in implementing innovative water recycling 
and reuse techniques, contributing to both resource 
efficiency and environmental stewardship.
	
Through the adoption of advanced water treatment 
technologies 
and 
robust 
monitoring 
systems, 
Himadri continues to reduce water consumption 
while protecting natural ecosystems—demonstrating 
our unwavering commitment to sustainable and 
responsible operations.

per the audit report.
5.	
Has the entity implemented a mechanism for Zero 
Liquid Discharge (ZLD)? If yes, provide details of its 
coverage and implementation
	
Yes, to support our wastewater recycling and Zero 
Liquid Discharge (ZLD) system, Himadri has established 
an advanced Water Recovery Plant (WRP)—the final 
recovery stage of our Effluent Treatment Plant (ETP). 
This innovative system is designed to maximize water 
reuse, minimize waste, and significantly reduce our 
reliance on freshwater resources.
	
The WRP receives treated wastewater from various 
sources, including the ETP, DM plant backwash, RO 
plant reject water, and cooling tower blowdown. 
These are collected in the WRP feed tank and 
then directed to a clarifier, where a carefully dosed 
combination of dolomite, polyelectrolyte, sodium 
hypochlorite, caustic, and coagulant helps settle 
Total Suspended Solids. The clarified, TSS-free water 
is then stored in a dedicated tank.
	
From here, the water undergoes several advanced 
filtration processes:
 
 
It is first passed through a Mixed Gravel Filter 
(MGF) with Hydrochloric Acid HCL dosing to 
eliminate any residual suspended solids.
 
 
Next, it enters an Ultrafiltration (UF) unit, which 
separates permeate and reject water into 
respective tanks.
 
 
The permeate water is then treated through a 
two-stage Reverse Osmosis (RO) system—first 
stage with five membranes, second stage with 
two—after pre-treatment using a carbon filter 
and dosing with HCL, sodium metabisulphite, 
and anti-scalant.
 
 
Before reaching the final permeate tank, the 
water passes through a De-Gasifier unit to 
remove excess carbon dioxide, ensuring stable 
pH levels.
	
Fig: ZLD process
	
The final permeate water, with a daily recovery of 
1200 KL, is effectively reused for cooling tower 
makeup, process requirements, and RO plant feed. 
Meanwhile, the final concentrate water amounting 
to 50 KL per day, is sustainably utilized in various 
places of our manufacturing unit. This integrated 
system 
showcases 
Himadri’s 
commitment 
to 
responsible water management by significantly 
reducing groundwater consumption and reinforcing 
our vision for sustainable industrial operations.

initiative aligns with our broader water conservation strategy and reinforces our commitment to sustainability. 
By enhancing ZLD capacity and implementing advanced water recycling systems, we have reduced water usage 
and operational costs, contributing to resource efficiency. This proactive approach positions Himadri as a leader 
in sustainable water management, ensuring compliance with regulatory standards while mitigating future water 
scarcity risks. This strategy not only drives cost savings but also enhances operational resilience against water-
related challenges.

Alongside emissions of greenhouse gases, energy generation and industrial production result in further emissions 
into the air. We want to reduce these further and therefore take the emissions situation into strategy development. 
Our clean air measures include returning exhaust gases to the production process, thermal processing of residual 
gases with a high calorific value, the use of electric filters to remove particulates, the use of catalysts to reduce 
nitrogen oxide, and desulfurization by washing with subsequent precipitation.

implemented a new innovative solution to reduce 
Particulate Matter (PM) 2.5 and 10 with PURE SKIES 
2.0. This was a successful initiative that reduced 
the levels of PM from the last year as shown in the 
above data set. Our company diligently strategizes 
to check, monitor and make significant initiatives 
to reduce the emission. Our Air Quality & Emission 
Control Policy are in place to execute the ESG related 
guidelines. 
 
 
The 
Vehicle 
Management 
Standard 
(Framework) implemented by Himadri plays a 
vital role in reducing air pollution. By ensuring 
that all vehicles within the plant premises are 
roadworthy and fully compliant with local 
regulations, particularly those governing the 
transport of hazardous materials, the Framework 
minimizes the emission of harmful pollutants. 
Regular pre-operation safety checks, combined 
with a robust preventative maintenance system, 
ensure that vehicles operate efficiently, resulting 
in lower pollutant emissions. The Framework 
also mandates strict adherence to speed limits 
and prohibits the use of mobile phones while 
driving, reducing the risk of accidents and 
unnecessary idling, both of which can contribute 
to air pollution. By maintaining vehicles in 
optimal condition and enforcing stringent 
operational protocols, Himadri significantly 
reduces pollutant emissions, supporting cleaner 
air and demonstrating its commitment to 
sustainability and environmental stewardship.
 
 
The Hot Material Vapour Scrubbing Unit is 
designed to remove certain components from 
gases or vapours by washing them with a liquid 
absorbent called wash oil. The liquid, enriched 
with absorbed constituents, is then replaced 
with fresh liquid. The scrubber unit uses a 
packed tower where the gas enters from the 
bottom and the scrubbing liquid enters from the 
top, leading to absorption and condensation of 
vapors. To maintain the liquid temperature, a 
cooling coil with circulating water is employed. 
The unit follows a daily checklist, monitoring the 
level and temperature of the scrubbing liquid. 
If the temperature exceeds the limit, the water 
inlet valve is adjusted. 
	
	
Additionally, the cloud point of the liquid is 
tested, and if it goes beyond the specified 
temperature, the liquid is replaced. The optimal 
level range of the scrubbing liquid is 40% 
to 60%, with a temperature range of 45°C to 
55°C and a cloud point of 35°C. To control 
vapour emissions from light oil tanks, a nitrogen 
blanketing system is installed, reducing air 
pollution. The nitrogen pressure is regulated to 
maintain controlled pressure inside the tank. If 
the pressure increases, the tank vent actuator 
releases the excess pressure to the atmosphere. 
On the other hand, if the pressure decreases, the 
nitrogen actuator opens to introduce nitrogen 
and maintain the set tank pressure. 
 
 
The presence of nitrogen in the tank reduces 
air pollution by exhausting nitrogen first during 
vapour release, leading to the condensation of 
light oil vapour into liquid inside the tank. The 
NOx Abatement Process at Himadri aims to 
reduce NOx emissions from the cellulose nitration 
reactors at the site. The process consists of two 
main components: a scrubber/absorber tower 
and a reaction vessel with a catalyst bed. The 
scrubber/absorber tower comes in contact with 
NOx-laden fumes with water, producing nitric 
acid through absorption. Moreover, we regularly 
monitor POP across all our plants.
Note: Indicate if any independent assessment/ 
evaluation/assurance has been carried out by an 
external agency? (Y/N) If yes, name of the external

Yes, Himadri undertakes thorough and regular 
evaluations of major air pollutants to ensure 
adherence to environmental standards and to protect 
public health. Third-party experts are engaged 
to perform independent assessments, enhancing 
the credibility and transparency of the monitoring 
process. Periodic quarterly audits are conducted to 
verify our performance regarding air pollutants such 
as NOx, SOx, and Particulate Matter (2.5 & 10) etc. 
These quarterly audit results are submitted to the 
regulators by the appointed third party. The audit 
also verifies the compliancy of our operations as set 
by the regulators such as Central Pollution Control 
Board of India. The periodic analysis of air pollutants 
not only helps in maintaining compliance but also 
supports Himadri’s commitment to environmental 
stewardship. We have also carried out assurance 
by TUV SUD South Asia Pvt Ltd. for current 
reporting year.

Does the entity have any project related to reducing

Yes, at Himadri, we fulfill 90% of our power 
requirements through our 28MWh capacity power 
plant, showcasing our dedication to environment 
preservation. To reduce waste gas and off-gas venting 
during carbon black production, we’ve implemented 
an innovative process that recirculates and feeds 
off-gas into power generation, significantly lowering 
Greenhouse Gas (GHG) emissions. Our power plant 
features three boilers that adequately meet the 
energy demands of our West Bengal unit, with surplus 
electricity being sold to the local grid. This Financial 
year we have sold about 82,954.53 MW electricity 
to the local grid. With our low emission factor in 
generation of electricity the total emission avoidance 
is reported at 19,909 tCO2e for FY 2024-25.

Limited 
has 
replaced the conventional fuel oil heating

480 Ton per day Coal Tar distillation project. 
This transition from a fuel oil heating system to 
a steam heating system has brought significant 
improvements in efficiency and effectiveness 
while lowering associated emission. The fuel 
required for dehydration has been eliminated, 
leading to a substantial reduction in GHG 
emissions. By switching to steam energy, the 
Company benefits from improved heating 
performance, potentially lower energy costs, 
reduced GHG emissions.

Setting the carbon price 
Approval and oversight 
Financial/ Investment decision 
Review and adjustment 
* Internal price for carbon, which is a fixed amountper ton of CO2e emitted 
* Internal price for carbon, which is a fixed amountper ton of CO2e emitted 
* Integration of carbon cost in return of investment calculation 
* Carbon cost acts as a shadow price for investment/capex on estimated Scope 1 and 2 GHG emissions 
* Periodic review to update price reflecting market dynamics and other factors
then applied to these emissions to calculate a "carbon cost," which is included in the overall cost-benefit 
analysis. This ensures that projects with lower carbon emissions are more financially attractive, incentivizing 
investments in more sustainable options. Himadri implements the shadow pricing mechanism in which we 
assign a monetary value to each ton of carbon dioxide. Shadow pricing mechanism is a crucial tool to ensure 
that the environmental implications of long-term investment decisions are fully understood. India being a fast-
becoming compliance market for emission. Himadri supports Paris Agreement on Climate Change objectives.

Himadri strongly believes in circularity and avidly 
implement, them in its operations. Circular economy 
task force drives Himadri’s efforts to embed circular 
economy 
principles 
throughout 
the 
business. 
By minimizing waste, promoting recycling and 
optimizing product lifecycles, this task force ensures 
that resources are used efficiently and sustainably. 
Through collaboration across departments and 
initiatives (take-back programs), the task force 
creates innovation and reduces environmental 
impact, contributing to a closed-loop system.
	
Himadri disposes the non-hazardous wastes (Plastic 
wastes, process and metal waste etc.) through PCB 
approved third party vendors. They recycle or reuse 
the wastes as per their authorization. Internal records 
are kept through SAP system.
	
Hazardous waste (ETP Sludge, Mixed waste, Cotton 
waste, Old insulation waste, Oil soaked jute and empty 
bags etc.) and also Bio-medical wastes segregated in 
the hazardous waste bin. These are disposed via PCB 
approved waste disposal third party. They dispose 
the waste by LAT (Landfilling after treatment) or 
Incineration procedure taking all the measures and 
maintaining proper regulations. All the records are 
kept as per regulation. HSE department keeps track 
of the whole procedure. Himadri being a responsible 
organization engages with these vendors as per our 
stakeholder engagement policy. The policy mandates 
audit protocols, SOP exchange, knowledge transfer, 
and capacity building as regular norms. 
	
Our commitment extends to ensure all the employees 
are well trained in appropriate waste handling and 
emergency procedures.

10.	 Briefly describe the waste management practices 
adopted in your establishments. Describe the 
strategy adopted by your company to reduce usage 
of hazardous and toxic chemicals in your products 
and processes and the practices adopted to manage 
such wastes.
Himadri’s efforts to reduce production waste are 
guided by a principle: avoid waste. If avoidance is 
not possible, waste should be recycled or used in 
energy generation. If recycling or energy generation 
is not feasible, waste should be disposed safely. The 
need to establish high-level circular economies that 
support sustainable economic growth is increasingly 
critical. Given the planet’s finite resources, rising 
lifestyle standards and growing resources demand on 
account of a rising global population, conventional 
one-way economic models will no longer be able 
to sustain prosperous lifestyles and cultures going 
ahead. To stimulate economic activity and move to 
a decarbonised society, it will be essential to reduce 
the use of fossil-based plastics while addressing 
a growing demand for plastics. In this context, 
Himadri acknowledges the growing importance 
of reducing plastic consumption and enhancing 
recycling. As a speciality chemical manufacturing 
Company, Himadri takes a comprehensive approach 
to identify risks associated with various types of 
waste, including production waste, packaging waste, 
plastics and wood pallets. The Company considers 
a range of plausible scenarios through consultations 
with internal and external stakeholders.
	
Process optimisation is central to Himadri. This 
includes 
in-plant 
reprocessing 
of 
substance 
streams and the application of the 3R principle 
(reduce, reuse, recycle) across operational sites. 
Where waste cannot be avoided, the focus is on 
mechanical or thermal reprocessing. At Himadri’s 
sites, various types of recyclable waste — plastics, 
glass, paper, food waste and wood—are segregated 
and dispatched to external recycling firms approved 
by regional pollution control boards. The Company 
monitors these firms through audits to ensure their 
corresponding compliance with statutory provisions.
	
Himadri adheres to the recommendations of state 
government waste management authorities related 
to handling hazardous wastes like effluent sludge, 
oil-contaminated gloves, jute and soak sand. It 
employs vendors authorised by the pollution 
control boards. The Company reintroduced recycled 
products as inputs following the end-of-life phase 
of its products. Himadri launched a pilot project to 
implement a reusable packaging solution, with the 
potential to eliminate plastics and wood from its 
packaging.
	
Besides, the Company strives to achieve its 
ambitious waste management target (zero waste to 
landfill). Himadri leverages the benefit of integrated 
production sites and systems for systematic waste 
management. By-products from one production 
process are repurposed as raw materials of other 
products, widening the value chain. The Company 
sources raw materials from other sectorial by-
products (coal tar and carbon black feedstock). In 
addition to reprocessing, waste with high calorific 
value (substitute fuel) is used to produce energy, 
reducing a reliance on primary fossil fuels and 
moderating Company’s carbon footprint. Himadri 
is exploring alternatives to replace virgin materials. 
Annexure IX 
of the Board's Report (Contd.)

This includes initiatives to replace fossil-based plastics with alternatives like paper and metal. The Company is 
progressing to use plant-based plastics as an alternative to fossil-based plastics. At Himadri, all plant waste and 
process scraps are systematically collected and transported to the main waste yard for segregation into hazardous 
and non-hazardous categories. Disposal of these wastes is carried out in compliance with Pollution Control Board 
(PCB) regulations and through PCB approved third-party vendors under the supervision of the Health, Safety 
and Environment (HSE) function. Himadri maintains regular communication with third-party vendors to monitor 
the final disposal and ensure proper management of the waste, reaffirming its commitment to environmental 
responsibility.

Himadri does not operate in any ecologically sensitive area. However, Himadri has established a well-maintained 
greenbelt as a natural barrier to mitigate noise pollution in and around its operational areas. This greenbelt, 
covering 33% of the facility’s total area as confirmed by external audits, is designed with dense plantations of 
native species that act as effective sound absorbers. Beyond noise reduction, the greenbelt also contributes to 
improved air quality, enhanced biodiversity, and aesthetic enrichment of the environment. Himadri’s commitment 
to sustainable practices is exemplified by this initiative, demonstrating a harmonious balance between industrial 
operations and environmental stewardship. We are also planning to commission a butterfly habitat in the plant to 
advance Himadri’s commitment towards preserving and promoting bio-diversity.

Financial Statements
	
Himadri has strengthened its climate action framework by formally including Scope 3 emissions in its greenhouse 
gas (GHG) accounting and disclosure process starting FY 2023–24. Recognising that a significant portion of its 
total emissions lies beyond its direct operations, this strategic inclusion marks a key milestone in Himadri’s journey 
towards comprehensive climate responsibility and alignment with global best practices.
	
The Company has undertaken a structured approach to Scope 3 management, beginning with detailed mapping 
of its value chain to identify hotspots and high-emission categories. Priority areas such as purchased goods and 
service, upstream transportation, and downstream transportation have been brought under focus for accurate 
data collection and emissions quantification. 
	
To drive meaningful impact, Himadri has set an ambitious yet achievable Scope 3 emission intensity reduction 
target of 5% by 2025, compared to its 2023 baseline. This target is aligned with the Science Based Targets initiative 
(SBTi) and supports the broader global goal of limiting temperature rise to below 1.5°C. It also reflects Himadri’s 
commitment to responsible growth by embedding sustainability deeper into its value chain.
	
Previously, industry average data were used to account Himadri’s Scope-3 emission. However, with the direction of 
our BoD members in this current year we embarked on a journey to enhance the granularity of data for a detailed 
emission profile. Therefore, praxis of data collection had been modified accordingly and Himadri launched a formal 
value chain engagement process. 
	
To ensure that sustainability is ingrained throughout our supply chain, Himadri employs a multi-stage process 
for evaluating Value Chain Partners. Each Value Chain Partner is required to complete a detailed self-assessment 
survey that covers ESG and other business aspects. Depending on the risk profile of each Value Chain Partner, we 
conduct either on-site or remote audits. These audits focus on key areas of performance, including environmental 
management, health and safety protocols, labor practices, and corporate governance. Then each Value Chain 
Partner is categorised on respective risk indexes and then corrective action plans are shared with the partners to 
mitigate any potential risk. As a environmentally conscious organisation Himadri takes a pro-active collaborative 
approach to carry out any environmental stewardship projects. One such initiative includes the planned shift from 
conventional diesel to biodiesel for both upstream and downstream logistics — a move that not only reduces 
emissions but also supports India’s national biofuel mission.  
	
By adopting this forward-looking and collaborative approach, Himadri is not only strengthening its Scope 3 
inventory but also fostering innovation and shared responsibility across the value chain. These efforts underline 
Himadri’s vision to lead by example in building a low-carbon, resilient and sustainable future for all stakeholders.
Note: Indicate if any independent assessment/evaluation/assurance has been carried out by an external agency? 
(Y/N) if yes, name of the external agency.
Yes, we have employed an independent third party to account our GHG emission. This particular assessment was 
carried out by TUV SUD South Asia Pvt Ltd. during the current reporting year. Accounting is done in accordance 
of methodologies detailed by Green House Gas Protocol which is a global standard.

If the entity has undertaken any specific initiatives or used innovative technology or solutions to improve resource

the same as well as outcome of such initiative:
Sl

Details of the initiative (web link if any, may be

Outcome of the initiative
1
Nitrogen blanketing
This system controls pressure and minimizes 
vapor emissions, helping to prevent air 
pollution. It employs nitrogen pressure to 
control emissions, significantly mitigating 
odors by condensing light oil vapors into 
liquid form. By creating an inert atmosphere 
inside storage tanks, nitrogen blanketing 
minimizes the presence of oxygen, which in 
turn reduces the evaporation of VOCs from 
the liquid surface.
Presently, vent out vapor mixture 
is rich with nitrogen as it is more 
volatile than light oil vapor as a 
result air pollution has reduced 
from before. As tank is under 
controlled pressure so that vapor 
mixture emission has reduced 
resulting in lowering air pollution.
2
Waste Heat 
Recovery : APH, 
OPH,WHRB & Dryer 
APH to reduce GHG 
emissions
The system enhances heat recovery by 
capturing heat from hot smoke and utilizing 
it to generate hot air. This recovered heat is 
then effectively used in the Oil Pre-Heater 
(OPH)and Captive Power Plant (CPP) boiler 
combustor.
As a result, Himadri has achieved 
a total energy usage of1.20 GJ/hr 
in OPH and 5.45 GJ/hr in CPP. This 
initiative optimizes the utilization 
of waste heat, contributing to 
improved energy efficiency 
and promoting environmental 
sustainability.
3
Sludge to fuel
Himadri’s initiative to implement a reduction 
process for internal waste, such as sludge, 
represents a significant step forward in 
sustainable waste management and resource 
recovery The conversion process adopted by 
Himadri focuses on transforming the sludge, 
a by-product typically produced during 
industrial operations, into a valuable resource. 
Through this innovative process, the sludge 
undergoes a transformation, turning it into a 
usable fuel.
This fuel can then be utilized 
in auxiliary operations, such as 
powering certain machine or 
serving as an alternative energy 
source for specific industrial 
activities. 
By harnessing the energy potential 
of sludge, Himadri is promoting 
a circular economy model where 
waste is minimized, and valuable 
resources are recovered and 
repurposed.
4
Reduction of PM2.5 
& PM10 –Clean Air 
Mission
The technology uses pulsed radio waves 
(WiFi) to accelerate the natural clearance of 
these microscopic pollutants. This technique 
coagulates PM2.5 and PM10 through pulsed 
radio waves which presents several potential 
benefits for air quality improvement. By 
causing the particulate matter to coagulate 
and settle, the concentration of harmful 
particles in the air is reduced.
Air quality typically improves 
by 30-40% or more, leading to 
improved health and reduced 
risk of non-compliance with air 
pollution norms.
5
Application of 
Anthracene Oil 
in Carbon Black 
Production
In the context of a circular economy, using 
Anthracene oil derived from coal tar as a 
feedstock for carbon black production is an 
innovative and sustainable approach that 
significantly contributes to resource efficiency 
and environmental sustainability.
By redirecting Anthracene oil 
into the carbon black production 
process, Himadri is not only 
creating a valuable industrial 
product but also closing the loop in 
the life cycle of coal tar derivatives, 
ensuring that fewer resources go 
to waste.

Outcome of the initiative
6
Yield Improvement 
in Carbon Black 
Production
Himadri is producing Carbon black by partial 
combustion of the Anthracene oil, this yield 
gain process also reduces the extraction of 
energy transformation as we are converting 
the higher volume of mass to the finish 
product, which will help to reduce energy 
loss and reduce GHG emission also. We have 
achieved the yield gain of 4% due to process 
excellence process.
The yield gain is a sustainable 
approach to reduce the raw 
material consumption to achieve 
circular economy initiatives as well 
as to reduce the carbon footprint.
7
Environmental 
Impact Reduction 
: 480 TPD Project 
–New RC-Coal Tar 
Division
Himadri has implemented a strategic 
approach to energy reduction by transitioning 
from a single-stage cooling system (Old RC) 
to an advanced double-stage cooling system 
(New RC). In the previous system, the total 
heat load was forwarded directly to the 
cooling tower, leading to higher energy and 
water consumption. With the New RC system, 
the total heat load is divided into two streams: 
one directed towards RO (Reverse Osmosis) 
water and the other towards the cooling 
tower.
This division significantly reduces 
the heat load on the cooling tower, 
resulting in lower evaporation 
losses—saving approximately 8 KL 
of water per day. Additionally, the 
New RC system improves energy 
efficiency by converting excess 
heat into steam, which is forwarded 
to the LP steam header for reuse.
5.	
Does the entity have a business continuity and disaster management plan? Give details in 100 words/ web link.
	
Himadri has developed a robust Business Continuity and Disaster Management Plan (BCDMP), which is integrated 
into the Company’s comprehensive Risk Management Policy. This forward-thinking plan is a testament to Himadri’s 
unwavering commitment to operational resilience, long-term value creation, and sustainable business growth, even 
in the face of unforeseen disruptions. Himadri has successfully conducted the Stage 1 audit for ISO 22301:2018, the 
international standard for Business Continuity Management Systems (BCMS). This audit marks a significant step in 
Himadri's commitment to ensuring the resilience and continuity of its operations.
	
The BCDMP serves as a strategic blueprint to ensure uninterrupted operations during natural calamities, industrial 
emergencies, cyber threats, and other potential disruptions. It reflects Himadri’s focus on protecting stakeholder 
value, enhancing corporate governance, and aligning with its long-term strategic objectives. The plan outlines 
procedures to maintain critical business functions, secure employee and community safety, and preserve 
environmental integrity—minimizing harm to people, infrastructure, biodiversity, and ecosystems.
	
Himadri’s approach to risk management is proactive and data-driven. All financial and non-financial risks are 
continuously identified, assessed, and mitigated under the guidance of the Risk Management Committee, 
a dedicated oversight body that reports directly to the Board. This includes climate-related risks, operational 
disruptions, supply chain vulnerabilities, and emerging ESG concerns.
	
To ensure that the BCDMP remains dynamic and effective, regular simulations, risk assessments, and audits are 
conducted. These evaluations help identify gaps, incorporate learnings, and update response protocols in line with 
evolving business environments and global best practices. Employees across critical functions are also trained to 
respond efficiently during emergencies, reinforcing a culture of preparedness and accountability.
	
Through this integrated and forward-looking risk governance framework, Himadri not only safeguards its assets 
and people but also ensures that it continues to deliver value to customers and communities—even in times of 
crisis. This resilience is fundamental to Himadri’s sustainable growth vision and its ability to thrive in an increasingly 
complex and interconnected world.

2.	
Provide details of corrective action taken or underway on any issues related to anti-competitive conduct by the 
entity, based on adverse orders from regulatory authorities.
	
Himadri’s fair competition policy ensures a compliance with anti-trust laws and promotes fair trade in accordance 
with guideline provided by Competition Commission of India. Employees are trained to recognise and avoid 
practices like price fixing or monopolistic behaviour. To detect non-compliance, the Company established strong 
vigilance mechanism and reporting channels that employees, personnel from staffing agencies working at its 
premises and external stakeholders to report compliance violations. We conduct frequent legal and ethical reviews, 
involving internal and external legal advisors. We implemented strict internal controls to detect and prevent any 
potential anti-competitive behaviour. All these measures helped us to achieve zero incidents of anti-competitive 
behaviour consistently.
	
Additionally, our Grievance Redressal policy which is publicly available, establishes an anonymous complain 
channel for all the stakeholders. Any stakeholder can reach us via any means such as email, phone call, or any 
such established mechanism. Anonymity of the complainant is ensured through the highest authority level of 
the company. Company Secretary, Chief Sustainability Officer, and Chief Human Resource Officer are part of the 
committee to oversee the grievances, its effective Redressal, and overall efficacy of our established mechanism.

Himadri’s Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR) programmes reflect our deep-rooted commitment to creating 
inclusive, meaningful, and lasting impacts in the communities we serve. With over three decades of purposeful 
engagement, our CSR initiatives go far beyond regulatory compliance—they are a reflection of our core values and 
dedication to social responsibility. Guided by a dedicated Board-level CSR Committee, each project is thoughtfully 
designed, meticulously planned, and closely monitored from inception to completion to ensure maximum impact. 
Aligned with the UN Global Compact (UNGC) principles and increasingly shaped by Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion 
(DEI) values, our efforts promote sustainable development, STEM education, and community empowerment.
	
Empowering Communities through Sports and Social Welfare: Himadri’s annual football tournaments foster unity 
and physical wellness, drawing crowds of nearly 6,000 spectators and offering youth a positive platform for 
growth. To support vulnerable populations during winter, we distributed warm clothing and blankets to residents 
across 20 villages, ensuring safety and comfort. Our skill development programmes equip women with vocational 
abilities, driving financial independence and improved household livelihoods.
	
Education and Infrastructure Support: Firm believers in the transformative power of education, we support 
students through scholarships and learning materials, benefitting over 400 students and distributing more than 
2,000 books. Infrastructure upgrades at Joymolla High School and Nasibpur Kishalaya Handicapped School have 
enriched the learning environment for over 1,700 students, including children with disabilities, promoting inclusivity 
and academic growth.
	
At Himadri, we see CSR as a cornerstone of our mission to build a sustainable and equitable future. By collaborating 
with local partners and responding to real community needs, we create shared value—empowering individuals, 
strengthening communities, and advancing a culture of purpose, inclusiveness, and integrity.

Principle 9
Businesses should engage with and provide value to their consumers in a 
responsible manner
SDGs Impacted
Businesses are responsible for providing safe products and services that 
have a minimal impact on society and the environment. Additionally, 
they must provide accurate and complete information about the 
products to facilitate informed decision-making for consumers and 
free competition in the market.
Customer centricity is at the heart of Himadri’s business strategy, 
reflected in active engagement to grasp evolving customer needs. The 
Company consistently strives to exceed expectations by delivering 
superior customer experiences. Himadri is committed to responsible 
customer data management and employing world-class systems to 
ensure data privacy and cybersecurity standards are upheld across 
its operations.
Essential Indicators
1.	
Describe the mechanisms in place to receive and respond to consumer complaints
100%
Resolution of feedback from 
customers
Nil
Number of Data 
Security Issues
	
At Himadri, we follow a structured and responsive approach to ensure that every customer concern is addressed 
promptly and effectively. When a complaint is raised, regional managers from the Marketing department register 
it, capturing essential details such as product and grade information, invoice number, nature of the issue, customer 
or agent details, and any supporting images. The complaint is immediately shared with the Head of Technical 
Services and the Head of Quality Control. Customers receive an acknowledgment from the Regional Marketing 
Manager, assuring them that their concern is being acted upon.
	
Within one working day, the Head of Technical Services forwards the complaint internally to the relevant department 
heads. These teams collect the necessary data and present their findings in a Corrective and Preventive Action 
(CAPA) meeting within two working days. Appropriate corrective steps are then initiated to resolve the issue. Once 
resolved, the outcome is communicated to the customer by the Marketing Manager. In cases where the complaint 
is found to be unjustified, the Head of Technical Services and Regional Marketing Manager engage directly with 
the customer to provide clarification and close the matter amicably.
	
The complaint closure form is completed by the Head of Technical Services and authorized by the Plant Head. If 
the resolution identifies any need for process improvements, necessary updates are made to procedures, work

instructions, or specifications. All complaints, along with detailed analysis and actions taken, are documented and 
maintained by the Head of Quality Control—ensuring transparency, accountability, and continuous improvement.

Himadri is deeply committed to protecting customer 
interests and promoting ethical business conduct, 
recognizing that consumer trust and satisfaction 
are foundational to long-term success. By upholding 
transparency, integrity, and accountability in all 
aspects of governance, Himadri fosters strong 
consumer confidence and reinforces its reputation 
as a responsible and customer-centric organization.
	
To ensure data protection, Himadri strictly adheres to 
both national and international regulations, including 
the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) and 
relevant local laws. All sensitive customer data is 
encrypted during transmission and securely stored 
using state-of-the-art technologies to prevent 
unauthorized access. The Company obtains explicit 
consent for data collection, processing, and storage, 
and follows a clear data retention policy that ensures 
information is not held longer than necessary and is 
disposed of securely.
	
Employees undergo regular training on cybersecurity 
awareness, ethical behavior, and data privacy best 
practices to ensure compliance with Himadri’s 
robust data protection policies. Periodic security 
audits are conducted to proactively identify and 
address vulnerabilities. A comprehensive information 
security due diligence conducted by TUV SUD South 
Asia Pvt Ltd. confirmed that there were no data 
breach incidents, underscoring the effectiveness 
of Himadri’s protocols. In addition, a well-defined 
Incident Response Plan is in place to swiftly detect, 
report, and respond to any potential cybersecurity 
incidents.
	
Himadri 
also 
maintains 
strong 
compliance 
with antitrust and fair competition laws. Its fair 
competition policy ensures that all transactions—
with customers, suppliers, and business partners—
are conducted transparently and in alignment with 
ethical standards. Pricing strategies are designed 
to be fair, competitive, and reflective of market 
dynamics. Regular audits of value chain partners 
ensure alignment with Himadri’s commitment to fair 
trade and responsible business practices.
	
A robust Whistle-blower Policy empowers all 
stakeholders to report unethical practices or 
violations without fear of retaliation. Independent 
audits further reinforce compliance with legal and 
ethical standards across all operations.
	
Through 
these 
rigorous 
measures, 
Himadri 
demonstrates 
its 
unwavering 
commitment 
to 
integrity, 
ethical 
governance, 
and 
customer 
protection—maintaining a record of zero complaints 
related to data breaches, unfair trade practices, or 
restrictive conduct.

Himadri strives to set a new benchmark in our 
industrial 
sector 
by 
underpinning 
sustainable 
practices to navigate through a diverse and dynamic 
global business landscape and maintain transparency 
in all our interactions. Himadri is aligned with the 
International Council of Chemical Associations’ 
(ICCA) global agenda through the Responsible 
Care® initiative, supported by the Indian Chemical 
Council, its Indian counterpart. This underlines the 
Company’s commitment to the highest standards of 
safety, health and environmental performance. We 
have implemented comprehensive quality control 
processes throughout the entire production life. We 
have conducted detailed audits of all our suppliers 
and vendors to ensure they met our high standards 
of product safety and quality. Our extensive product 
trials and testing including real-world consumer 
testing wherever applicable have helped to identify 
potential safety concerns. Our adherence to ISO 
certifications and safety laws, is rigorously followed in 
all stages of design, manufacturing and distribution. 
Additionally, all our customers are supplied with 
comprehensive product MSDS which clearly outlines 
all the safety parameters starting from handling to 
safe disposal.

Himadri has successfully achieved zero incidents 
related 
to 
data 
breaches 
through 
a 
strong

comprehensive measures in line with international 
standards. This achievement is largely attributed 
to Himadri's proactive risk management strategies, 
which include regular security audits, encryption 
and multi-layered access controls. Himadri has 
conducted a thorough data security due diligence 
process by TUV SUD South Asia Pvt Ltd. a globally 
recognized certification body which also assured 
clients and stakeholders that Himadri is committed 
to protecting sensitive information and mitigating 
potential data security risks.

2.	
Steps taken to inform and educate consumers 
about safe and responsible usage of products and/
or services.
    Himadri, as part of its commitment to consumer safety 
and responsibility, has implemented a series of steps 
to   educate and inform its consumers about the safe 
and responsible usage of its products and services.
	
1.	
Clear and detailed product labeling/MSDS: 
Himadri ensures that all products come with 
clear & easy to understand labelling that 
outlines usage instructions, safety precautions 
and potential hazards.
	
2.	
Comprehensive user manuals and guidelines: 
These resources often include visual aids and 
step-by-step instructions.
	
3.	
Customer support and helplines: Himadri has 
set up dedicated customer support teams and 
helplines to offer guidance and provide safety 
related information to consumers.
	
4.	
Online resources and FAQs: Himadri maintain 
an 
online 
resource 
center 
that 
includes 
frequently asked questions (FAQs), safety tips, 
troubleshooting guides and product usage 
videos.
	
5.	
Product training and demonstrations: Himadri 
offers product demonstrations, either in-person 
or via virtual platforms, to show consumers the 
correct way to use its products.
	
6.	
Awareness 
programs: 
Himadri 
sponsors 
awareness campaigns across various platforms, 
focusing on the safe and responsible use of its 
products.    
3.	
Mechanisms in place to inform consumers of any risk 
of disruption/discontinuation of essential services.
	
Information related to any risk of disruption/
discontinuation of essential services is communicated 
to consumers through e-mails, phone calls or any 
such established media.
